CC   -!- FUNCTION: Endo-1,4-beta-xylanase involved in the hydrolysis of
CC       xylan, a major structural heterogeneous polysaccharide found in
CC       plant biomass representing the second most abundant polysaccharide
CC       in the biosphere, after cellulose. Accounts for approximately 70
CC       percent of the endoxylanase activity in the culture filtrate.
CC       {ECO:0000269|Ref.2}.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Endohydrolysis of (1->4)-beta-D-xylosidic
CC       linkages in xylans. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:8589407}.
CC   -!- PATHWAY: Glycan degradation; xylan degradation.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted {ECO:0000269|PubMed:8589407}.
CC   -!- INDUCTION: Expressed in presence of rice cell walls or on oat
CC       spelt xylan, but not when grown on sucrose.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:8589407}.
CC   -!- DISRUPTION PHENOTYPE: Retains 39 percent of the catalytic
CC       activity. Double xyl1/xyl2 deletion mutant retains 19 percent of
CC       the activity and exhibits a 50 percent reduction in accumulation
CC       of total mycelial mass. {ECO:0000269|Ref.2}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the glycosyl hydrolase 10 (cellulase F)
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 GH10 (glycosyl hydrolase family 10) domain.
CC       {ECO:0000255|PROSITE-ProRule:PRU01096}.

CC   -!- ENZYME REGULATION: Metal ions, copper, iron and N-bromosuccinimide
CC       decrease enzyme activity. Manganese, calcium, L-tryptophan, beta-
CC       mercaptoethanol, L-cysteine and dithiodipyridine stimulate the
CC       enzyme activity. {ECO:0000269|Ref.4}.
CC   -!- BIOPHYSICOCHEMICAL PROPERTIES:
CC       pH dependence:
CC         Optimum pH is 5.0. Retains about 76 percent of its activity
CC         after being incubated at pH 2.0 for 30 min at 37 degrees
CC         Celsius. {ECO:0000269|Ref.4, ECO:0000269|Ref.5};
CC       Temperature dependence:
CC         Optimum temperature is 50 degrees Celsius. Displays about 95
CC         percent of peak activity in the temperature range from 37 to 41
CC         degrees Celsius. {ECO:0000269|Ref.4, ECO:0000269|Ref.5};

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Hydrolyzes 1,4-beta linked polysaccharide backbones of
CC       xylans, one of the major hemicellulose components in hardwoods and
CC       softwoods. It is more active against xylopentaose than
CC       xylotetraose, has trace activity against xylotriose. The major
CC       products released from hydrolysis of xylooligosaccharides are
CC       xylobiose and xylotriose. The reiterated 40 AA domain is involved
CC       in binding the cellulase-hemicellulase complex.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Endohydrolysis of (1->4)-beta-D-xylosidic
CC       linkages in xylans.
CC   -!- PATHWAY: Glycan degradation; xylan degradation.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: Consists of an N- and C-terminal catalytic domains linked
CC       to a middle reiterated domain. Only the C-terminal catalytic
CC       domain is active.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the glycosyl hydrolase 11 (cellulase G)
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.
